### Post by labinnsw on 2010-04-30
Guess it is up to me again

Rules:

1. Stay within the board rules, no matter how hot you may believe the wallpaper/screen shot to be.
2. If you are going to quote, there isn't a need to quote an img-embeded picture - Just don't do it. Please just reference the post by page number/page link/etc.
3. Off Topic Posts will be edited or removed.
4. The desktops thread is not to be used as a means to post explicit or suggestive, and provocative images (they must be safe for your kids and/or boss to see). Please help to keep the thread relevant and safe to browse for everyone.
5. The moderators of this forum reserve the right to edit or remove your posts as necessary so they may comply with our Community Rule set.
6. Please use reduced-size thumbnails, out of respect for people running on lower bandwidth or screen resolutions.
7. To avoid having users having to ask you for them. when possible we request that you format your posts in the following order: NOTE this is optional

Themes: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).
Wallpaper: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).
Icons: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).
Programs: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

**Important Note: Any image posted that is over 800 x 600 will be removed! Use a thumbnail or use a text link to your image. If your image is removed, this is why.**

### Post by CrimsonBizarre on 2010-05-01
> **cespinal said:**
> how do you achieve that panel ala windows 7? looks pretty

[Dock Bar X]("http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/DockbarX?content=101604"), and using a Main Menu button as oppose to the standard Menu Bar.

Remove the gnome-panel at the top and make the bottom one around 37-42 pixels high.

I'm using [Glassified]("http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Glassified+theme+for+DockbarX+0.21.11?content=109283") Dock Bar X theme, but [Shinybar]("http://levviathor.deviantart.com/art/Shinybar1-3-for-DockbarX-135875506") theme replicates Windows 7's superbar, and includes a panel background that looks like the aero-style used by Windows 7.

Hope that helps. :)
[_[U]_[/U]]("http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/DockbarX?content=101604")

### Post by koleoptero on 2010-05-05
Edited the Ambiance-NautilusMod theme to be dark. I just thought that Ambiance looks really good fully dark but when changing the colours from the appearance preferences some things just looked wrong (buttons for one). I also purged the orangeness of various things and made them purple for less contrast.

Theme attached for anyone interested. Constructive and/or destructive criticism is always welcome.

[[IMG]http://farm5.static.flickr.com/4054/4580220285_4e1d4ce464.jpg[/IMG]]("http://farm5.static.flickr.com/4054/4580220285_73e24e38fa_o.png")

[[IMG]http://farm5.static.flickr.com/4068/4580851432_e091953f1c.jpg[/IMG]]("http://farm5.static.flickr.com/4068/4580851432_02db0a4bdc_o.png")

[[IMG]http://farm5.static.flickr.com/4023/4580220613_bb63a5d98e.jpg[/IMG]]("http://farm5.static.flickr.com/4023/4580220613_9e112913fb_o.png")

EDIT: Posted it on gnome-look.org too: [http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php?content=124199](http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php?content=124199)

### Post by matty-guy on 2010-05-06
> **5dolla said:**
> is that open box? if so how do you install it in ubuntu. guess i could install #! but its built on debian now instead of ubuntu.

Just because #! isn't on ubuntu doesn't mean you cant give it a try. Even if you dislike it, its never bad to try out more systems and gain more knowledge on how they work. If you want openbox on the system you have now, download the latest version, install it, and run 'openbox --replace'. This'll change the window manager, however nautilus still controls the desktop, so then you'd have to go to run 'gconf-editor' and navigate to nautilus in there somewhere, un-tick the box that says nautilus handles the desktop, and then find a way to remove the gnome-panel in favour of tint2 if you want to go that far. I had issues when I stopped nautilus handling the desktop but my problem doesn't seem to have happened with many other people.

---

### Post by chickengirl on 2010-05-06
> **matty-guy said:**
> Just because #! isn't on ubuntu doesn't mean you cant give it a try. Even if you dislike it, its never bad to try out more systems and gain more knowledge on how they work. If you want openbox on the system you have now, download the latest version, install it, and run 'openbox --replace'. This'll change the window manager, however nautilus still controls the desktop, so then you'd have to go to run 'gconf-editor' and navigate to nautilus in there somewhere, un-tick the box that says nautilus handles the desktop, and then find a way to remove the gnome-panel in favour of tint2 if you want to go that far. I had issues when I stopped nautilus handling the desktop but my problem doesn't seem to have happened with many other people.

Or, if you want to dive right in - install openbox, logout, then switch your session to openbox (there's a dropdown menu on the login screen to do that). You'll pretty much get a black screen. Don't panic. ;) You can build up your own desktop from there using whatever components you want, and none of the ones you don't. :)

---

### Post by chickengirl on 2010-05-06
> **Mykle87 said:**
> Nice openbox. Are you just using gnome-power-manager and gnome-volume-control? I'm looking for ideas for building openbox from a command-line install.

This is my autostart.sh:

```
thunar-volman &
thunar --daemon &
gnome-power-manager &
update-notifier &
nitrogen --restore &
padevchooser &

(sleep 2 && tint2) &
nm-applet &
blueman-applet &
pidgin &
conky &
```

padevchooser is a pulseaudio tray applet thing. the rest should be pretty self-explanatory.

### Post by koleoptero on 2010-05-07
**@Rasa1111:** Go to system -> preferences -> startup applications
Add a new one by clicking add at the side, and in the command field add /home/YOUR_USERNAME/.init-conky
replace of course the YOUR_USERNAME with your actual username.

**@bra|10n:** This script already has a bash script starting it with a delay.

---

### Post by slackthumbz on 2010-05-07
> **Ringi said:**
> I need more information, dock howto and icons :)
heh, the dock is AWN
search for avant in the software center and install the dock (avant-window-navigator) and all the plugin packages for it. Tweaking and customisation is really easy in AWN. The icons are from the ACYL set which can be found here: [http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Any+Color+You+Like?content=102435]("http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Any+Color+You+Like?content=102435")

### Post by slackthumbz on 2010-05-07
> **Ringi said:**
> Not for me :)
How do you get this curve on left side of the dock?

Go to the theme tab in the dock settings and click 'Customise' at the bottom. The settings for the curve are under 'numerical settings' (see the screenshot for mine). Also I've set my dock style to 'Edgy' in the general preferences.

### Post by CrimsonBizarre on 2010-05-08
I'm intrested in Docky - what makes it so great? I'm not trying to say I think that it is bad or anything, but I can't see what it has over other Docks.

I'm currently using AWN, I think it's pretty great. I can put my launchers on there and use them easily enough, and the new feature: 'docklets' is amazing. The 'places' one for example; you click the folder and your launchers are replaced by places such as 'home', and 'pictures', I only wish that you can put seperators between launchers.

Docky. Same basic features as AWN, though lacks the 'docklets' feature that make applets a lot more interesting and dynamic. The Gnome DO version of Docky is slightly better, the whole dock acts as the frontend for DO, and so you can open web pages, programs, etc, just my searching, but I don't really see the point in that - if you need quick access to things, should they not already be on your dock? Plus, the DO version lacks features the stand-alone version has, and the stand-alone version lacks all DO features.

I'd like to see more applets for both. They both have media player controllers, for example, AWN's in the form of a 'docklet', but they both only work with Rhythmbox (I use Exaile), and AWN's version only displays album art from IDv3 tags and not Metadata (or something like that. It never states that, yet when I organise all of my music, using winamp in windows, I only apply the album art to the Metadata, and usually leave the IDv3 and IDv2 tags alone and only certain music comes with album art in those tags - so only certain music appear with album art in the applet - but I could be wrong and it could be a bug.)

---

### Post by Minipalmer on 2010-05-08
> **CrimsonBizarre said:**
> I'm intrested in Docky - what makes it so great? I'm not trying to say I think that it is bad or anything, but I can't see what it has over other Docks.I love AWN and Gnome-Do. At one point I was using both. But I like AWN as a panel more than a dock. Have you tried the new AWN rewrite from PPA? It has a panel mode that is beautiful. I used it instead of gnome-panel for a long time on Karmic.

With AWN I loved having the "Places" applet that you mentioned, as well as the terminal applet that let me have a little mini-terminal in the panel. Made things simple.

But you're right, Docky seems about the same as Gnome-Do. I like Gnome-Do because the dock gathers all of your most used launchers, and also is the most intuitive launcher for Gnome IMO. Maybe Docky is for people who want the dock but not Gnome-Do?

---

### Post by ogregore on 2010-05-09
Lucid with my changes:

Wallpaper = found on wallbase.net (color searched for "purple").
Theme = Ambiance
Metacity = My Ambiance (with right hand buttons & center title).
Icons = Ubuntu Mono-dark (with some personal changes such as "start-here").
Conky = new lucid theme conky with minor additions such as minimal weather.

[[IMG]http://img697.imageshack.us/img697/3169/screenshot1sn.th.png[/IMG]]("http://ubuntuforums.org/[URL=http://img697.imageshack.us/i/screenshot1sn.png/)%20%20Uploaded%20with%20[ImageShack.us](http://imageshack.us)"][[IMG]http://img697.imageshack.us/img697/3169/screenshot1sn.th.png[/IMG]](http://img697.imageshack.us/i/screenshot1sn.png/) [/URL]

### Post by TakezoB on 2010-05-09
> **CrimsonBizarre said:**
> How did you get nautiilus like that?

and what web browser is that?

Thanks :)

Nautilus is just elementary-nautilus + beadcrumps (check out this link : [http://www.webupd8.org/2010/04/nautilus-elementary-breadcrumbs-for-any.html](http://www.webupd8.org/2010/04/nautilus-elementary-breadcrumbs-for-any.html)).

The Web Browser is simply Epiphany. With the theme(aire gtk from TheValrog),emerald, and icons(Moblin) it makes it look neat. Faster than firefox, and more elegant. :)

### Post by PhilGil on 2010-05-11
> **armageddon08 said:**
> Can somebody tell me how can I make the panel applet for tomboy monochrome?
I would start by uninstalling the Tomboy panel applet, as the monochrome Tomboy icon is part of the indicator applet (I assume having the panel applet installed suppresses the icon in the indicator applet).  If the monochrome icon still doesn't appear then I would try logging out and logging back in again.  If the Tomboy icon still doesn't appear there may be a command to add it to the indicator applet, otherwise you'll have to restore your panel to the default settings.

---

### Post by cguy on 2010-05-13
> **Brutal cake said:**
> Nice desktop. :) Could you post the color scheme, please?

Thanks! :)

- Oxygen widget theme
- Obsidian Coast color scheme, but with the Window background #BBBBBB
- the Desktop theme is Air, but with the widget & translucent background from Oxygen
- the clock is "Slim glow"

I also cleaned up the title bar by removing the unnecessary buttons (close, minimize and maximize) :D

### Post by Daisuke_Aramaki on 2010-05-13
> **gutterslob said:**
> Pure Class!!
Would you mind sharing your .Xdefaults, Dai-chan?.... or at least the rxvt colour-scheme.
Currently contemplating an all white setup, but I'm still undecided on whether I should take a multi-coloured or multiple-shades-of-grey approach for the terminals. Yours would be a big help.


Thanks man. Sure thing. Here are a couple of variations that you can use as a starting point

Setup1

```

!Thayer-Lightr
!black
URxvt*color0:    #555555
URxvt*color8:    #000000
!red
URxvt*color1:    #ff005f
URxvt*color9:    #ff00af
!green
URxvt*color2:    #008700
URxvt*color10:   #00af00
!yellow
URxvt*color3:    #ff8700
URxvt*color11:   #ffaf00
!blue
URxvt*color4:    #000087
URxvt*color12:   #0000ff
!magenta
URxvt*color5:    #870087
URxvt*color13:   #af00d7
!cyan
URxvt*color6:    #0087af
URxvt*color14:   #00afd7
!white
URxvt*color7:    #709080
URxvt*color15:   #1e2320
```

Setup2

```

!Mod
URxvt*color0:     rgb:00/00/00
URxvt*color1:     rgb:d4/00/00
URxvt*color2:     rgb:22/a2/1f
URxvt*color3:     rgb:fb/66/0a
URxvt*color4:     rgb:43/8e/c3
URxvt*color5:     rgb:ff/00/86
URxvt*color6:     rgb:00/86/d2
URxvt*color7:     rgb:69/69/69
URxvt*color8:     rgb:70/79/6b
URxvt*color9:     rgb:ff/00/07
URxvt*color10:    rgb:22/a2/1f
URxvt*color11:    rgb:fd/89/00
URxvt*color12:    rgb:43/8e/c3
URxvt*color13:    rgb:ff/00/86
URxvt*color14:    rgb:00/86/f7
URxvt*color15:    rgb:55/44/44
```

### Post by K.Mandla on 2010-05-15

---

### Post by koleoptero on 2010-05-15
> **K.Mandla said:**
> That was probably me. :oops:

Still ... 100Mb on startup is a bit high for my tastes. To each his own though. ;)

I know  it was you, I was just joking. :D Although it's not only you. But when I saw you had the last post I just had to say it. :D

I can understand why you would think 100mbytes are a lot for startup ;) (which increases exponentially when launching firefox+pidgin) but what I've noticed is that in xubuntu the cached things in ram (which I suppose are the * in htop) are much less than in ubuntu. Ubuntu will start swapping when I reach 400mbytes of used ram or more, while xubuntu doesn't.

It still isn't the most lightweight xfce-based distro out there (#! xfce uses about 50 mbytes at startup according to something I've read somewhere) but it's enough for users with five year old hardware.

### Post by koleoptero on 2010-05-16
> **gutterslob said:**

...and gasp!!... you're using Exaile!! O_O

Thanks m8. Yeah exaile now works quite well, and I wanted a music player/organizer that can do ratings and auto playlists. Rhythmbox looks auful, banshee is too heavy (not bloated for what it does, but heavy for what I want) and mono dependant, amarok is... well amarok, and the list goes on. After trying everything out I decided to go *back* to exaile that behaves properly in this version (I used to be a fan of exaile two versions back).

Also I want to use complex and not simple wallpapers from now on, because I won't be using conkies, docks, and all the things that make a desktop complicated by themselves. LOL

.conkyrc
```

# -- Conky settings -- #
background no
update_interval 1
 
cpu_avg_samples 2
net_avg_samples 2
 
override_utf8_locale yes
 
double_buffer yes
no_buffers yes
 
text_buffer_size 2048
imlib_cache_size 0
 
# -- Window specifications -- #
 
own_window yes
own_window_type normal
own_window_transparent yes
own_window_hints undecorate,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager,below
 
border_inner_margin 0
border_outer_margin 0
 
minimum_size 320 800
maximum_width 320
 
alignment bottom_right
gap_x 0
gap_y 0
 
# -- Graphics settings -- #
draw_shades no
draw_outline no
draw_borders no
draw_graph_borders yes
 
# -- Text settings -- #
use_xft yes
xftfont MaiandraGD:size=24
xftalpha 0.4
 
uppercase no
 
default_color 888888
 
# -- Lua Load -- #
lua_load ~/.lua.lua
lua_draw_hook_pre ring_stats
 
TEXT
${alignr}${voffset 53}${goto 90}${font MaiandraGD:size=11}${time %A, %d %B %Y}


${voffset 5}${goto 164}${font MaiandraGD:size=16}${time %H:%M}



${voffset -40}${goto 100}${font MaiandraGD:size=9}Kernel:${offset 70}Uptime:
${goto 90}${font MaiandraGD:size=9}$kernel${offset 40}$uptime 
${voffset 57}${goto 117}${font snap:size=8}${cpu cpu0}%
${goto 117}${cpu cpu1}%
${goto 117}CPU
${voffset 19}${goto 145}${memperc}%
${goto 145}$swapperc%
${goto 145}MEM
${voffset 25}${goto 170}${acpitemp} C
${goto 170}TEMP
${voffset 27}${goto 198}${downspeed eth0}
${goto 198}${upspeed eth0}
${goto 205}NET
${voffset 21}${goto 222}${fs_used /}
${goto 222}${fs_used /home}
${goto 230}DISK

```
.lua.lua
```
--[[
Ring Meters by londonali1010 (2009)
 
This script draws percentage meters as rings. It is fully customisable; all options are described in the script.
 
IMPORTANT: if you are using the 'cpu' function, it will cause a segmentation fault if it tries to draw a ring straight away. The if statement on line 145 uses a delay to make sure that this doesn't happen. It calculates the length of the delay by the number of updates since Conky started. Generally, a value of 5s is long enough, so if you update Conky every 1s, use update_num > 5 in that if statement (the default). If you only update Conky every 2s, you should change it to update_num > 3; conversely if you update Conky every 0.5s, you should use update_num > 10. ALSO, if you change your Conky, is it best to use "killall conky; conky" to update it, otherwise the update_num will not be reset and you will get an error.
 
To call this script in Conky, use the following (assuming that you save this script to ~/scripts/rings.lua):
	lua_load ~/scripts/rings-v1.2.1.lua
	lua_draw_hook_pre ring_stats
 
Changelog:
+ v1.2.1 -- Fixed minor bug that caused script to crash if conky_parse() returns a nil value (20.10.2009)
+ v1.2 -- Added option for the ending angle of the rings (07.10.2009)
+ v1.1 -- Added options for the starting angle of the rings, and added the "max" variable, to allow for variables that output a numerical value rather than a percentage (29.09.2009)
+ v1.0 -- Original release (28.09.2009)
]]
 
settings_table = {
	{
		-- Edit this table to customise your rings.
		-- You can create more rings simply by adding more elements to settings_table.
		-- "name" is the type of stat to display; you can choose from 'cpu', 'memperc', 'fs_used_perc', 'battery_used_perc'.
		name='time',
		-- "arg" is the argument to the stat type, e.g. if in Conky you would write ${cpu cpu0}, 'cpu0' would be the argument. If you would not use an argument in the Conky variable, use ''.
		arg='%I.%M',
		-- "max" is the maximum value of the ring. If the Conky variable outputs a percentage, use 100.
		max=12,
		-- "bg_colour" is the colour of the base ring.
		bg_colour=0x888888,
		-- "bg_alpha" is the alpha value of the base ring.
		bg_alpha=0.3,
		-- "fg_colour" is the colour of the indicator part of the ring.
		fg_colour=0x888888,
		-- "fg_alpha" is the alpha value of the indicator part of the ring.
		fg_alpha=0.5,
		-- "x" and "y" are the x and y coordinates of the centre of the ring, relative to the top left corner of the Conky window.
		x=191, y=145,
		-- "radius" is the radius of the ring.
		radius=32,
		-- "thickness" is the thickness of the ring, centred around the radius.
		thickness=4,
		-- "start_angle" is the starting angle of the ring, in degrees, clockwise from top. Value can be either positive or negative.
		start_angle=0,
		-- "end_angle" is the ending angle of the ring, in degrees, clockwise from top. Value can be either positive or negative, but must be larger (e.g. more clockwise) than start_angle.
		end_angle=360
	},
	{
		name='time',
		arg='%M.%S',
		max=60,
		bg_colour=0x888888,
		bg_alpha=0.3,
		fg_colour=0x888888,
		fg_alpha=0.5,
		x=191, y=145,
		radius=37,
		thickness=4,
		start_angle=0,
		end_angle=360
	},
	{
		name='time',
		arg='%S',
		max=60,
		bg_colour=0x888888,
		bg_alpha=0.3,
		fg_colour=0x888888,
		fg_alpha=0.5,
		x=191, y=145,
		radius=42,
		thickness=4,
		start_angle=0,
		end_angle=360
	},
	{
		name='cpu',
		arg='cpu0',
		max=100,
		bg_colour=0x888888,
		bg_alpha=0.3,
		fg_colour=0x888888,
		fg_alpha=0.5,
		x=140, y=300,
		radius=26,
		thickness=5,
		start_angle=-90,
		end_angle=180
	},
	{
		name='cpu',
		arg='cpu1',
		max=100,
		bg_colour=0x888888,
		bg_alpha=0.3,
		fg_colour=0x888888,
		fg_alpha=0.5,
		x=140, y=300,
		radius=20,
		thickness=5,
		start_angle=-90,
		end_angle=180
	},
	{
		name='memperc',
		arg='',
		max=100,
		bg_colour=0x888888,
		bg_alpha=0.3,
		fg_colour=0x888888,
		fg_alpha=0.5,
		x=170, y=350,
		radius=26,

	},
	{

		arg='',

		fg_colour=0x888888,
		fg_alpha=0.5,
		x=170, y=350,
		radius=20,

	},
	{
		name='time',
		arg='%d',

	},

	},
	{
		name='fs_used_perc',
		arg='/',
		max=100,

		fg_colour=0x888888,
		fg_alpha=0.5,

	},
	{
		name='fs_used_perc',
		arg='/home',
		max=100,
		bg_colour=0x888888,
		bg_alpha=0.3,
		fg_colour=0x888888,
		fg_alpha=0.5,
		x=260, y=503,
		radius=20,
		thickness=5,
		start_angle=-90,
		end_angle=180
	},
	{
		name='upspeedf',
		arg='eth0',
		max=50,
		bg_colour=0x888888,
		bg_alpha=0.3,
		fg_colour=0x888888,
		fg_alpha=0.5,
		x=230, y=452,
		radius=20,
		thickness=5,
		start_angle=-90,
		end_angle=180
	},
	{
		name='downspeedf',
		arg='eth0',
		max=100,
		bg_colour=0x888888,
		bg_alpha=0.3,
		fg_colour=0x888888,
		fg_alpha=0.5,
		x=230, y=452,
		radius=26,
		thickness=5,
		start_angle=-90,
		end_angle=180
	},
	{
		name='acpitemp',
		arg='',
		max=100,
		bg_colour=0x888888,
		bg_alpha=0.3,
		fg_colour=0x888888,
		fg_alpha=0.5,
		x=200, y=401,
		radius=26,
		thickness=6,
		start_angle=-90,
		end_angle=180
	},
}
 
require 'cairo'
 
function rgb_to_r_g_b(colour,alpha)
	return ((colour / 0x10000) % 0x100) / 255., ((colour / 0x100) % 0x100) / 255., (colour % 0x100) / 255., alpha
end
 
function draw_ring(cr,t,pt)
	local w,h=conky_window.width,conky_window.height
 
	local xc,yc,ring_r,ring_w,sa,ea=pt['x'],pt['y'],pt['radius'],pt['thickness'],pt['start_angle'],pt['end_angle']
	local bgc, bga, fgc, fga=pt['bg_colour'], pt['bg_alpha'], pt['fg_colour'], pt['fg_alpha']
 
	local angle_0=sa*(2*math.pi/360)-math.pi/2
	local angle_f=ea*(2*math.pi/360)-math.pi/2
	local t_arc=t*(angle_f-angle_0)
 
	-- Draw background ring
 
	cairo_arc(cr,xc,yc,ring_r,angle_0,angle_f)
	cairo_set_source_rgba(cr,rgb_to_r_g_b(bgc,bga))
	cairo_set_line_width(cr,ring_w)
	cairo_stroke(cr)
 
	-- Draw indicator ring
 
	cairo_arc(cr,xc,yc,ring_r,angle_0,angle_0+t_arc)
	cairo_set_source_rgba(cr,rgb_to_r_g_b(fgc,fga))
	cairo_stroke(cr)		
end
 
function conky_ring_stats()
	local function setup_rings(cr,pt)
		local str=''
		local value=0
 
		str=string.format('${%s %s}',pt['name'],pt['arg'])
		str=conky_parse(str)
 
		value=tonumber(str)
		if value == nil then value = 0 end
		pct=value/pt['max']
 
		draw_ring(cr,pct,pt)
	end
 
	if conky_window==nil then return end
	local cs=cairo_xlib_surface_create(conky_window.display,conky_window.drawable,conky_window.visual, conky_window.width,conky_window.height)
 
	local cr=cairo_create(cs)	
 
	local updates=conky_parse('${updates}')
	update_num=tonumber(updates)
 
	if update_num>5 then
		for i in pairs(settings_table) do
			setup_rings(cr,settings_table[i])
		end
	end
end
```
tint2rc
```
# Background definitions
# ID 1
rounded = 0
border_width = 1
background_color = #888888 14
border_color = #000000 26

# ID 2
rounded = 1
border_width = 1
background_color = #888888 66
border_color = #000000 20

# ID 3
rounded = 1
border_width = 1
background_color = #888888 26
border_color = #000000 20

# ID 4
rounded = 7
border_width = 1
background_color = #000000 66
border_color = #000000 100

# Panel
panel_monitor = all
panel_position = bottom center horizontal
panel_size = 100% 36
panel_margin = 0 0
panel_padding = 0 0 0
panel_dock = 0
wm_menu = 0
panel_layer = bottom
panel_background_id = 1

# Panel Autohide
autohide = 0
autohide_show_timeout = 0.0
autohide_hide_timeout = 0.0
autohide_height = 0
strut_policy = none

# Taskbar
taskbar_mode = single_desktop
taskbar_padding = 10 0 10
taskbar_background_id = 0
#taskbar_active_background_id = 0

# Tasks
urgent_nb_of_blink = 7
task_icon = 1
task_text = 0
task_centered = 1
task_maximum_size = 50 36
task_padding = 10 3
task_background_id = 3
task_active_background_id = 2
task_urgent_background_id = 4
task_iconified_background_id = 3

# Task Icons
task_icon_asb = 100 0 0
task_active_icon_asb = 100 0 0
task_urgent_icon_asb = 50 0 0
task_iconified_icon_asb = 100 0 0

# Fonts
task_font = kroeger 06_55 6
task_font_color = #222222 100
task_active_font_color = #000000 100
task_urgent_font_color = #FFFFFF 100
task_iconified_font_color = #FFFFFF 100
font_shadow = 0

# System Tray
systray = 1
systray_padding = 0 4 5
systray_sort = ascending
systray_background_id = 0
systray_icon_size = 0
systray_icon_asb = 100 0 0

# Clock
time1_format = %I:%M %p
time1_font = snap 7
time2_format = %d %b
time2_font = snap 7
clock_font_color = #000000 100
clock_padding = 10 3
clock_background_id = 0

# Tooltips
tooltip = 1
tooltip_padding = 10 10
tooltip_show_timeout = 0.1
tooltip_hide_timeout = 0.1
tooltip_background_id = 4
tooltip_font = snap 8
tooltip_font_color = #FFFFFF 66

# Mouse
mouse_middle = close
mouse_right = iconify
mouse_scroll_up = toggle
mouse_scroll_down = shade

# Battery
battery = 0
battery_low_status = 20
battery_low_cmd = notify-send "battery low"
battery_hide = 90
bat1_font = Sans 12
bat2_font = Sans 12
battery_font_color = #FFFFFF 100
battery_padding = 0 0
battery_background_id = 0

```

Sure :)  It`s Openbox window manager installed on Ubuntu command-line(without desktop envirement and applications) system. I use Slim as login manager, Pcmanfm as file manager and Tint2 as panel. Information in top left corner is conky. Application in the left bottom corner is Covergloobus. All themes/configs modified by me. Enjoy!

### Post by Islington on 2010-05-18
> **screaminj3sus said:**
> I almost want to install kde right now after seeing this screenshot, nice.

Thanks :) mission accomplished.

> **cespinal said:**
> Nice as always Is. 

Are you still using desktop grid (expo) for window navigation?

I am, since I am not happy with any of the taskbars atm. Also I am forcing certain windows to open on certain desktops on the grid so its super useful when combined with having similar windows autotabbing themselves.

> **ibuclaw said:**
> Wow, how easy is it to reproduce that from a vanilla KDE Desktop look?
SUPER EASY! since almost everything in there is defaults.

Step 1. Install bespin from svn, in bespin config import avanti.bespin from /*[whereever you built it]/cloudcity/presets/

2: Segoe Semibold Slight Antialias size 9 for all fonts except the mono (consolas) and window title (Segoe Bold size 9)

3. Panel on top, plasmoids: xbar, application launcher, digital clock, quick access, pager. 

4. Panel on the side make it really wide. Add the plasmoids: rssnow, weather, system tray, optional if you have space: system monitor. Put panel on autohide.

5. Wallpaper here: [Interfacelift Link]("http://interfacelift.com/wallpaper_beta/details/2225/cherry_flowers.html")

6. In systemsettings>> appearance> windowdecorations>> finetuning>> check the outline active window title.

7. Plasma theme: Ember, get it through systemsettings>> appearance>> style>> workspace tab>> get new themes

8. optional mess around with your bespin config, possibly enable toolbuttons with same coloring as buttons: in bespin> buttons>> toolbuttons. optional mess around with kwin buttons:systemsettings>> appearance> windowdecorations>>buttons>>custom positions for buttons.

> **rkakkar said:**
> how can i get my default kde installation to look like that in kubuntu?
glad you like it, I also run kubuntu see above.

> **Aspergillus said:**
> Stunning!!

what plasma theme is that?
Thanks :) plasma theme is called Ember, you can get it from the get new themes button.

---

TEXT
${image ~/Pictures/image.png}
$hr etc...
The attached pic is at 80% but you could use 20% if you like

### Post by Giant Speck on 2010-05-19
[[IMG]http://i279.photobucket.com/albums/kk122/SpecKtacle/th_Screenshot-58.png[/IMG]]("http://i279.photobucket.com/albums/kk122/SpecKtacle/Screenshot-58.png")

I've decided to do what I did when I first created Macchiato:  I'm going to use a different theme as a base.  Macchiato was originally my attempt to combine Dust with the color scheme of Glow Ibex.  Eventually, the theme became its own entity, and it has taken off from there.

Right now, I'm experimenting with using the Sugar theme as a new base for Macchiato.  For now, all I've done is brought the Macchiato color scheme over and squared the otherwise round features of Sugar, so that it looks more like Macchiato than Sugar.

Screenshot details:

GTK:  Macchiato (Sugar fork)
Emerald:  Macchiato Glass (custom, not yet available)
Font:  AvantGarde LT CondMedium 8
Icons:  Eikon (with some modifications)
Panel:  DockbarX with custom theme
Wallpaper:  custom (available [here]("http://i279.photobucket.com/albums/kk122/SpecKtacle/blue4.jpg"))

---

### Post by Mazza558 on 2010-05-19
I've wished for a desktop this simple for a long, long time. Thanks to AWN's customisability, I now have *the* perfect layout (IMO). I have an auto-hidden AWN panel which serves as a complete replacement of the boring gnome panel. A backup auto-hidden gnome panel appears if I keep the mouse at the top of the screen for 3 seconds, with a backup plan if awn crashes (like force-quit applet, sys monitor, etc).

Gnome-do is powerful enough for me to do anything else I want, so I can just relax and get on with stuff.

Thanks for that fantastic wallpaper, by the way!

### Post by Sealbhach on 2010-05-20
> **armageddon08 said:**
> Changing the font in Firefox does not change the font for all pages. For example, I changed it to Droid Sans in Firefox. While Wikipedia displays the content in the specified font, Ubuntu Forums still uses Sans.

In Firefox Preferences, if you click on the "Advanced" button, next to the default font selection box, you can tick whether to allow web pages to choose their own fonts or not. That works for me.

Like this:

[IMG]http://imgur.com/chwRK.png[/IMG]

.

### Post by ibuclaw on 2010-05-21
> **Ringi said:**
> Is there a hidden meaning in this sculpture :confused:

If you want the story behind it, my Laptop graphics card (NViDIA 8400GS) malfunctioned indefinitely this week. As part of the effort to replace it, have decided to replace the current HDD in the laptop with a new SSD, in a bid to keep the temperature down in the laptop as a whole. The HDD has been a known issue for quite some time, emitting 60-70C temperatures with little effort on my part.

There is only one thing stopping me from opening up the laptop though to get this done. There is a stripped screw preventing the lifting of the HDD to get access to the rest of the unit. What makes it even more of a nuance is that this is a very particularly small screw too (about 3mm in length, and 2mm width).

The image was taken to demonstrate to a friend just how small the screw was, by stacking it ontop of a standard desktop screw, which is either a 6mm or 8mm, I forget which one. :)

So yeah, I got a bit artsy in my emphasis of it's size. He still remains persistent that he can remove it. If only I could get to Ohio... ;)


Full image here if anyone wants to gimplify it.
[http://img200.imageshack.us/img200/7012/dsc0009bx.jpg](http://img200.imageshack.us/img200/7012/dsc0009bx.jpg)


(edit):
And here is another image I showed him.
[http://img192.imageshack.us/img192/8495/dsc0003qb.jpg](http://img192.imageshack.us/img192/8495/dsc0003qb.jpg)

### Post by bra|10n on 2010-05-21
ibuclaw your hesitancy here suggests you're not a "fiddler". But I know you can get this done and without needing to go to Kansas like Dorothy either ;)

For this particular situation, the main weapon in a fiddlers arsenal is a fast tapered knife or blade slipped under the screw head (if loose enough). It will depend on whether the screw head is seated into a recess or not,  though by the pics you've posted it seems this is not the case.  I say fast tapered knife or blade meaning it thickens away from the cutting edge rather quickly, allowing upward pressure or leverage if you will to be maintained whilst turning. A few turns is all it will take.

Just some thoughts...

---

### Post by tad1073 on 2010-05-21
> **Rasa1111 said:**
> I agree!

Can I get that also?
and how would I put it to use?  lol *hides face*
well done! :KS

> **Little Bones said:**
> I agree that it should be default, it looks great! Would you be able to post or send me that icon? Thanks.

look in /usr/share/icons/ubuntu-mono-dark/actions/24/
copy it to /usr/share/icons/<TheIconThemeYouAreUsing>/places/24/ for system wide 
and /home/yourname/.icons/24/ for local, rename the stock start-here.svg to start-here.svg then rename the new icon to start-here.svg and reload your icon theme

### Post by Little Bones on 2010-05-21
> **Rasa1111 said:**
> haha, 
i agree, yer beautiful...
but Im going back in my cave.....
confused as ever..... :lol:

The icon is here -> /usr/share/icons/ubuntu-mono-dark/actions/24/

Then copy it to-> /usr/share/icons/<TheIconThemeYouAreUsing>/places/24/  
-This will make it system wide (i.e. for every user) if you put it in "/home/yourname/.icons/24/" then it will just be for your account.

Rename the default start-here.svg  icon to start-here.svg.bak. Then rename the new icon to start-here.svg and reload  your icon theme.

Bit better?

### Post by Calixte on 2010-05-26
[http://lh6.ggpht.com/_qsozSSkVtUw/S_0kTKzQk8I/AAAAAAAAAJk/-NJr7ZDePQQ/Ubuntu-Screenshot-1.png](http://lh6.ggpht.com/_qsozSSkVtUw/S_0kTKzQk8I/AAAAAAAAAJk/-NJr7ZDePQQ/Ubuntu-Screenshot-1.png)
[http://***************/_qsozSSkVtUw/S_0kTeYlDbI/AAAAAAAAAJo/SSeJ9oFE7JE/Ubuntu-Screenshot-2.png](http://***************/_qsozSSkVtUw/S_0kTeYlDbI/AAAAAAAAAJo/SSeJ9oFE7JE/Ubuntu-Screenshot-2.png)

**Themes:** Ambiance (Ubuntu 10.04 default) with a slightly modified color theme
**Wallpaper:** Ubuntu 10.04 default with a superimposed symbol
**Icons:** Default
**Programs:** Chromium apps (Google Wave, Gmail, Facebook), Rythmbox, OpenOffice.org word processor, Movie Player, Nautilus File manager, AWN and Docky (see below)

The lower dock is **Docky** set on autohide with air theme, the left one is **AWN** (Avant Window Navigator) set on intellihide with the Dust theme and set on "edgy" style To get the round thing on the corner)
I also removed the bottom panel and slightly changes the top one.

**Compiz-Fusion Settings:**
- Click on top side and drag to get cover flow of applications on current workspace (gets a lot of *OMG-how-do-you-do-that?s* from non-geek friends)
- Bottom-right corner zoom out and view workspaces
- Bottom left: click to view current windows in "exposé" mode (right click = all windows, left-click = only current workspace)

### Post by x-shaney-x on 2010-05-27
> **$teve said:**
> what menu is this?

It is MintMenu, the default menu used in Linux Mint and in my opinion the the best menu there is.  I just can't go back to the horrid gnome menu anymore.

Anyhoo, you can add the mint repo as I do (though disable it after installing the menu) or follow the guide here: [http://www.webupd8.org/2010/05/install-linux-mint-main-menu-mintmenu.html](http://www.webupd8.org/2010/05/install-linux-mint-main-menu-mintmenu.html) 
Second method is probably less hassle though it might not be as up to date

### Post by 206bruce on 2010-05-27
[IMG]http://hphotos-snc3.fbcdn.net/hs466.snc3/25602_1373797913975_1502610157_926107_4358203_n.jpg[/IMG]

Design focus of my desktop is functionality.  I run three virtual desktops with edge flipping (w/ zero delay) by moving my mouse to the edge of the screen (via Compiz). The three main programs I run takes up most of the screen on each virtual desktop.  That's why every thing you see in my screenshot is off to the edge or corner.  They are also group accordingly.  I also don't have to do any mouse click to get to each of my program.  End result; speed, minimalistic, lots of screen real-estate.

Standard Ubuntu 9.10 Human theme, wallpaper, and HighContrast SVG icons
[Circle Clock Screenlet]("http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Circle+Clock?content=77159") 
[Wide Weather Screenlet]("http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Wide+weather?content=77168") 
[Conky system monitor with Lua scripts by londonali1010]("http://blog.conky.be/2009/10/19/widgets-in-conky-it-can-be-done/")
[AWN dock 0.3]("http://code.google.com/p/avant-window-navigator/")

### Post by x-shaney-x on 2010-05-28
> **thomasboleyn said:**
> That looks pretty nice. Very similar to the latest mint menu. How configurable is it?
Not very configurable unless you get into system files to alter things.
Also, the worst thing about gnome main menu is that if you click on more applications, it opens a window (looks a bit like gnome control centre).

A menu that opens a window to select an app?  I really don't get that.
It's ok to use alongside the menu bar so it allows easy access to your favourites (or you could just edit gnome menu to add a "favourites" sub-menu).

---

@szadek_
Yup, it's conky. An old style conky, I'd say.

@Ringi
That's damn nice.
Mind sharing some details on the GTK?
As for the conkyrc you requested, I did a reinstall and didn't keep the config. Reason was because I realized the SSD was a bit overkill for this system, and moved it to my main work rig, so I'm just making uses of a standard 7200rpm HDD now (more than fast enough considering how light and speedy this version of #! is)
As for specs of the system; like I said, built from leftover parts, so it's not that special compared to my main rig.... Quad core 2.66GHz, 4GB RAM, GeForce 9400GT... that's it, basically. ### Post by dzon65 on 2010-05-31
> **gutterslob said:**
> I actually prefer your version (just one letter for each)
Nice job! :)



Very nice. :)
Not often one sees a Gnome panel in OpenBox, though. O_o
Would you mind sharing that conky rc?
I know it's pretty easy to replicate, but I'm lazy. :P
Thanks in advance.

Thanks.About the gnome-panel.This a minimal install packed with leightweight stuff.Since the panel was there,might as well use it.And in fact,it doesn't use much more resources than ,say,lxpanel.
Here's the conkyrc.I have to tell you though (not sure I'm the only one) but the ram's not given the exact ram.That is,it shows far more than what's being used,I think due to the fact that it shows the cache as well.

# Configuration de Conky
#
# la liste des variables a été enlevée de ce fichier en faveur
# de la documentation.
# Visitez [http://conky.sf.net](http://conky.sf.net) pour une liste à jour.

# La "zone de texte" est la fenêtre Conky (et non uniquement le texte).

# Mettez yes si vous voulez que Conky soit intégré à l'arrière plan
background yes

# Police de X quand Xft est désactivé, vous pouvez en choisir une avec le programme xfontsel
#font 5x7
#font 6x10
#font 7x13
#font 8x13
#font 9x15
#font *mintsmild.se*
#font -*-*-*-*-*-*-34-*-*-*-*-*-*-*

# Utiliser Xft?
use_xft yes

# Police de Xft quand Xft est activé
xftfont Radio Space:size=8

# Texte alpha quand Xft est utilisé
xftalpha 0.8

# MPD hôte/port
# mpd_host localhost
# mpd_port 6600
# mpd_password tinker_bell

# Tout imprimer vers console ?
out_to_console no

# Boîte mail (? : mail spool)
mail_spool $MAIL

# Intervalles de mises à jour en secondes
update_interval 0.50

# Ceci est le nombre de fois que Conky va se mettre à jour avant de quitter
# Mettre à zéro pour faire tourner en permanence
total_run_times 0

# Créer sa propre fenêtre au lieu d'utiliser le bureau (requis dans Nautilus) ?
own_window yes

# Si own_window est sur yes, vous pouvez utiliser les options normal, desktop ou override
own_window_type normal

# Utiliser le fond transparent avec own_window ?
own_window_transparent yes

# Si own_window_transparent est sur no, vous pouvez changer la couleur de fond ici
own_window_colour hotpink

# Si own_window est sur yes, ces options du gestionnaire de fenêtre peuvent être utilisées
own_window_hints undecorated,below,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager

# Utiliser le double buffering (réduit le scintillement, peut ne pas fonctionner avec tout le monde) ?
double_buffer yes

# Taille minimum de la zone de texte
minimum_size 150 100

# Dessiner les ombres ?
draw_shades no

# Dessiner les contours ?
draw_outline no

# Dessiner les bordures autour du texte ?
draw_borders no

# Dessiner les bordures autour des graphes ?
draw_graph_borders no

# Longueur des traits des séparateurs
stippled_borders 10

# Marge entre la bordure et le texte
border_margin 4

# Épaisseur de la bordure
border_width 1

# Couleur par défaut et couleur de la bordure
default_color white
default_shade_color black
default_outline_color black


# Espace entre les bords d'écran et le texte
# same thing as passing -x at command line (aucune idée de comment traduire ceci)
gap_x 12
gap_y 60

# Soustraire les buffers du système de fichiers de la mémoire utilisée (? :subtract file system buffers from used memory) ?
no_buffers no

# Mettez yes si vous voulez que tout le texte soit en majuscules
uppercase no

# Nombre d'échantillons CPU pour faire la moyenne
# Mettre sur 1 pour désactiver la moyenne
cpu_avg_samples 2

# Nombre d'échantillons réseau pour faire la moyenne
# Mettre sur 1 pour désactiver la moyenne
net_avg_samples 2

# Forcer UTF8 ? À noter que le support UTF8 requiert XFT
override_utf8_locale no

# Ajouter des espaces pour empêcher les objets de partir n'importe où ? Ceci affecte seulement certains objets
use_spacer none

# Autoriser chaque moniteur de port à suivre au plus tant de connections (si 0 ou not est mis, le nombre par défaut est 256) ?
#max_port_monitor_connections 256

# Nombre maximum d'objets spéciaux, ex : polices, décalages, alignements, etc. Pas bien compris ça moi...
#max_specials 512

# Taille maximum du buffer utilisateur pour le texte, c'est à dire sous la ligne TEXT
#max_user_text 16384

# Intervalle de mise à jour pour le démon du lecteur de musique, ex : mpd, audacious
#music_player_interval 3

# La variable est donnée soit au format $variable soit au format ${variable}. Cette dernière
# permet les caractères justes après la variable et doit être utilisée dans les
# trucs du réseau à cause d'un argument.

# Ce qui est placé après 'TEXT' apparaîtra à l'écran.


# Alignement du texte, les autres options possibles sont expliquées (sûrement sur le site web)
alignment top_left
#alignment top_right
#alignment bottom_left
#alignment bottom_middle
#alignment top_middle
#alignment middle_left
#alignment middle_right
#alignment bottom_right
#alignment none


TEXT
${color #FF8000}SYSTEM ${color #232323}${hr 2}

${color #1992D6}CPU1: ${color #D4D5DB}${cpu cpu1}% ${alignr}
${cpubar cpu1 7,200}

${color #1992D6}CPU2: ${color #D4D5DB}${cpu cpu2}% ${alignr}
${cpubar cpu2 7,200}

${color #1992D6}RAM: ${color #D4D5DB} $memperc% ${alignr}
${membar 7,200}

${color #FF8000} HD ${color #232323}${hr 2}

${color #1992D6}${voffset -5}Home:
${voffset 4}${color #D4D5DB}${fs_free /home}/${fs_size /home} ${alignr}
${color #D4D5DB}${fs_bar 7,200 /home}
${if_mounted /media/disk}/80Gio   ${fs_used /media/disk}/${fs_size /media/disk}${alignr}${fs_used_perc /media/disk}%
${fs_bar /media/disk}
$endif
${color lightgrey}I/O disque :${color #D4D5DB} $diskio $color
${diskiograph 30,200 D4D5DB D4D5DB}

${color #D4D5DB}Highest CPU $alignr CPU% MEM%
${top name 1}$alignr${top cpu 1}${top mem 1}
${top name 2}$alignr${top cpu 2}${top mem 2}
${top name 3}$alignr${top cpu 3}${top mem 3}

${color #D4D5DB}Highest MEM $alignr CPU% MEM%
${top_mem name 1}$alignr${top_mem cpu 1}${top_mem mem 1}
${top_mem name 2}$alignr${top_mem cpu 2}${top_mem mem 2}
${top_mem name 3}$alignr${top_mem cpu 3}${top_mem mem 3}

${color #FF8000}NETWORK ${color #232323}${hr 2}${color}

${color #D4D5DB}Down ${downspeed eth0} k/s ${alignr}Up ${upspeed eth0} k/s
${downspeedgraph eth0 25,100} ${alignr}${upspeedgraph eth0 25,100}
Total ${totaldown eth0} ${alignr}Total ${totalup eth0}


${color #1992D6}Signal: ${color #D4D5DB}${wireless_link_qual_perc wlan1} ${wireless_link_bar wlan1}

${color #FF8000}SYNAPTIC ${color #232323 }${color #232323}${hr 2}
${color #D4D5DB}${execi 1800 aptitude search "~U" | wc -l | tail} Updates


${color #FF8000}TIME ${color #232323}${hr 2}
${color #D4D5DB}${alignc 17}${font Arial Black:size=16}${time %H:%M}${font}


One more thing,the only two themes installed are both clearlooks.I want to keep everything down (about 2.1 Gb).Here's the other one:[http://dzon65.deviantart.com/](http://dzon65.deviantart.com/)
